From here, that they disagree. Even if you say it does not disagree, there were tunnels and they were hidden. That is what is written (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Lamentations 3:9" href="/Lamentations.3.9"><i>Thr</i>. 3:9</a>): “He fenced my way with ashlar, my paths he destroyed.”
Rebbi Jonah in the name of Rebbi Zeïra: Even a vineyard reaching to the wall was redeemed<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">This explains what “outside the walls” means in the Mishnah.</i>.
Rebbi Aḥa said, this implies that the Temple will be rebuilt before the kingdom of David’s dynasty<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">Since the decree, according to R. Yose, mentions only the rebuilding of the Temple and not the coming of the Messiah, it implies that the two events are independent of one another.</i> as it is written (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 32:14" href="/Deuteronomy.32.14"><i>Deut</i>. 32:14</a>): “From the blood of a grape you will drink as wine”<sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote">This is an allusion to the explanation of this verse, describing the plenty induced by the Temple, either in <i>Sifry</i> <i>Deut</i>. 317: You will not have to work to press and make wine, but bring it in on a wagon, put it in a corner, and drink from it as from a barrel; or in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ketubot 111b" href="/Ketubot.111b">Babli <i>Ketubot</i> 111b</a>: It teaches you that each grape will produce 30 barrels of wine; read (following a pronunciation which has the same sound for  ָֿ and  ַ̇) חָמֶר as חֹמֶר (30 <i>seah</i>); cf. <i>Peak</i> 7:4.</i>. And you say so!
It was stated: Rebbi says, the House of Shammai said this only for the Sabbatical year, but in all other years of the Sabbatical cycle, the House of Shammai say that it is subject to a fifth and subject to removal. According to that Tanna, they learned the rules of the fourth-year orchard only from Second Tithe; since you say that there is no Second Tithe in the Sabbatical year, so there is no fourth-year orchard in the Sabbatical year. But then should there be no holiness in it? Its holiness comes from the verse (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 19:24" href="/Leviticus.19.24"><i>Lev</i>. 19:24</a>): “Holy for praises,” it has the status of those holy fruits over which praises are said. And should it be permitted to the fresh mourner? It is stated: This implies that it is forbidden to the fresh mourner. And should it be subject to removal? Following Rebbi Simeon, since Rebbi Simeon frees it from removal. And should it be redeemed while still connected to the ground?
Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel stated: Both in the Sabbatical year and in the rest of the years of the Sabbatical cycle, the House of Shammai say, there is no fifth and no removal. According to that Tanna, they did not at all learn the rules of the fourth-year orchard from Second Tithe. But then should there be no holiness in it? Its holiness comes from the verse (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 19:24" href="/Leviticus.19.24"><i>Lev</i>. 19:24</a>): “Holy for praises;” it has the status of those holy fruits over which praises are said. And should it be permitted to the fresh mourner? It is stated: This implies that it is forbidden to the fresh mourner. And should it be subject to removal? Following Rebbi Simeon, since Rebbi Simeon frees it from removal. And should it be redeemed while still connected to the ground?
Rebbi Zeïra asked before Rebbi Abbahu: From where that it needs redemption? (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 19:24" href="/Leviticus.19.24"><i>Lev</i>. 19:24</a>) “Holy for praises,” holy for redemption. The rabbis never refrain from explaining ה by ח.
Rebbi Ayvu bar Naggari stated before Rebbi La following Rebbi Ismael (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 27:31" href="/Leviticus.27.31"><i>Lev</i>. 27:31</a>): “If a man redeems part of his tithes, he should add their fifth to it.” That excludes the fourth-year orchard; one is not obligated by it for a fifth. Then he turned around and stated: There are two terms of redemption, one for the Second Tithe and one for the fourth-year orchard.
There we have stated: Rebbi Jehudah says, there is no vineyard in the fourth year for the Gentile, but the Sages say there is. Rebbi Eleazar said, so says the Mishnah: There is never a vineyard in the fourth year for the Gentile. Rebbi Bibi said before Rebbi Zeïra in the name of Rebbi Eleazar: According to the opinion of Rebbi, the statement of Rebbi Jehudah turns out to be like the statement of the House of Shammai. Since the House of Shammai said that they learned the rules of the vineyard of the fourth year only from Second Tithe; since you say that there is no Second Tithe in the Sabbatical year, so there is no fourth-year orchard in the Sabbatical year. Similarly, Rebbi Jehudah said that they learned the rules of the vineyard of the fourth year only from Second Tithe; since you say that there is no Second Tithe in Syria, so there is no fourth-year orchard in Syria. He said to him, look what he said! He said only, it is not subject to a fifth and is not subject to removal, hence, it is subject to all other rules; Rebbi Jehudah says, there is no vineyard in the fourth year for the Gentile in Syria.
Samuel bar Abba asked: Since the House of Shammai said that they learned the rules of the vineyard of the fourth year only from Second Tithe; since you say that there is no Second Tithe in the Sabbatical year, there is no fourth-year orchard in the Sabbatical year. Similarly, in the third and sixth years of the Sabbatical cycle, since there is no Second Tithe, there should not be any fourth-year orchard. Rebbi Yose said, even though there is no Second Tithe in the third and sixth years, there are the tithes. In the Sabbatical year, there are no tithes at all.
Ḥeipha asked: Since Rebbi Jehudah said that they learned the rules of the vineyard of the fourth year only from Second Tithe; since you say that there is no Second Tithe in Syria, there is no fourth-year orchard in Syria. Similarly, they learned the rules of the heave of the thanksgiving sacrifice only from the heave of the tithe; since you say that there was no heave of the tithe in the desert, will it follow that there was no heave of the thanksgiving sacrifice in the desert? Rebbi Yose said, they learned from it only in regard to quantities.
It was stated: Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Jehudah said, Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon said, Israel did become obligated for the fourth-year orchard only after 14 years, seven during which they conquered and seven during which they divided up the land. Rav Ḥisda said, it turns out that the argument of Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Jehudah is identical with that of his father Rebbi Jehudah. Just as Rebbi Jehudah said that they learned the rules of the fourth-year orchard only from Second Tithe, since you say that there is no Second Tithe in Syria, so there is no fourth-year orchard in Syria. Similarly, Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Jehudah said that they learned the rules of the fourth-year orchard only from Second Tithe, since you say that they did become obligated for the fourth-year orchard only after 14 years,, similarly there was no fourth-year orchard until after 14 years. Rebbi Yose said, he follows his son’s argument; Syria was inferred from “after 14 years;” “after 14 years” was not inferred from Syria.
It is written (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 19:25" href="/Leviticus.19.25"><i>Lev</i>. 19:25</a>): “In the fifth year, you shall eat its yield to add for you, etc.” Rebbi Yose the Galilean says, here one adds the fruits of the fifth to the fruits of the fourth year. Just as the fruits of the fifth year are for the proprietors, so the fruits of the fourth year are for the proprietors. Rebbi Zeïra, Rebbi Yasa, in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: It turns out that Rebbi Yose the Galilean argues like Rebbi Jehudah. Just as Rebbi Jehudah makes it his property, so Rebbi Yose the Galilean makes it his property.
Rebbi Jeremiah asked before Rebbi Zeïra: According to those who declare it his property, should it not be subject to tithes? He said to him, according to what Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said, as Rebbi Abin said in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi, not only this practice, but in any practical question which is weak in court and you do not know how to decide, go out and see how the public acts, and act accordingly. And we see that they do not give. Rebbi Mana said, that is, if the practice would follow the House of Shammai. But is there any public that acts according to the House of Shammai? Rebbi Abin said, they learned the rules of the vineyard of the fourth year only from Second Tithe; just as you say that Second Tithe is not subject to tithes, so the yield of the fourth year is not subject to tithes.
Rebbi Abba, Rebbi Ḥiyya, in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: A dough of Second Tithe in Jerusalem, following Rebbi Meïr, is free from <i>ḥallah</i>, following Rebbi Jehudah it is subject to <i>ḥallah</i>. Rebbi Jonah said, they said this only for Jerusalem, but not for the countryside.
Rebbi Abba bar Cohen asked before Rebbi Yose: Does he who declares it obligated for single berries also declare it obligated for <i>ḥallah</i>? He said to him, is that not Rebbi Jehudah? And it is our opinion that in all this practice, Rebbi Jehudah follows the House of Shammai.

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> How does one redeem a fourth-year orchard? He puts a tetradrachma<sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote">Most Mishnah mss. read הסל “the basket” but in addition to the Leyden ms. the reading here is in a ms. of the Babli and in a Mishnah ms. from the Geniza. Therefore, it does not seem permissible to treat the reading here as a scribal error.</i> before three [experts] and asks, how much does a person redeem for himself for a tetradrachma when all expense<sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">The entire expense for growing this year’s yield.</i> is on him? Then he puts down the money and says, all that is collected under this is exchanged for this money; so and so many baskets per tetradrachma.<br>In a Sabbatical, he redeems its full value<sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote">Since there is no agricultural work, no costs accrue that could be deducted.</i>. If all of it was abandoned<sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote">In a non-Sabbatical year, the amount invested before it was abandoned is not deductible by the person who acquires the ownerless property; he may only deduct his own expenses of harvesting.</i>, he has only the cost of harvesting. He who redeems a fourth-year orchard adds its fifth whether it was his or was given to him as a gift<sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote">Following the House of Hillel, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Maaser Sheni 5:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Maaser_Sheni.5.2.1">Mishnah 3</a>. If it was given as a gift it becomes the recipient’s property only if delivered before the time of heave and tithes since later the yield is Heaven’s property.</i>.<br>The removal<sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote">The removal is the same as for Sabbatical produce (<i>Ševi‘it</i> 9:8); no produce may remain in the hands of the owner. {Maimonides holds that the leftovers have to be burned.}</i> was on the day before the first<sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote">This is the reading of both Yerushalmi mss. and a majority of the Mishnah mss. However, the Cambridge ms. of the Galilean Mishnah as well as the Maimonides autograph read “last” day; and this reading is necessary in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Maaser Sheni 5:5:2-7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Maaser_Sheni.5.5.2-7">Halakhah 7</a>. In <i>Sifry Deut</i>. 302, the mss. are divided about evenly between “first” and “last”. One might speculate that the reading “first” is derived from some mss. in which יום טוב אחרון was abbreviated to י״ט א׳ which was read as י״ט אחד (ראשוֹן).</i> day of Passover in the fourth and the seventh year [of the Sabbatical cycle.] What is the removal? One gives heave and heave of the tithe to its recipients<sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote">The Cohanim.</i>, First Tithe to its recipients<sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">The Levites.</i>, tithe of the poor to its recipients. Second Tithe and First Fruits are removed on the spot<sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote">Outside of Jerusalem, they cannot be eaten. If anything is left, it must be destroyed. This rule shows that in Jerusalem one needs the entire holiday of Passover to dispose of Second Tithe.</i>. Rebbi Simeon says, first fruits one gives to the Cohanim like heave. A cooked dish the House of Shammai say one has to remove, but the House of Hillel say it is as if removed<sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote">This sentence seems to have been part of the next Mishnah since it is discussed at the beginning of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Maaser Sheni 5:3:10-4:9" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Maaser_Sheni.5.3.10-4.9">Halakhah 6</a>.</i>.<br>He who had produce<sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote">Of Second Tithe. Since there is no Temple, the tithe cannot be eaten in Jerusalem. The House of Shammai hold that <a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 14:25" href="/Deuteronomy.14.25">Deut. 14:25</a> requires that any tithe produce which cannot be eaten in purity in the holy precinct has to be exchanged for money. Since that money cannot be used it must be destroyed or safely buried. The House of Hillel, the authors of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Maaser Sheni 1:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Maaser_Sheni.1.3.1">Mishnah 1:5</a>, hold that either the coins must be destroyed or the produce left to rot.</i> in this time and the year of removal came, the House of Shammai say he has to exchange it for money; the House of Hillel say, either money or produce.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> To redeem for a tetradrachma [means] he buys for himself for a tetradrachma. “He has only the cost of harvesting” including the cost of removing the pedicles<sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote">And any post-harvest processing needed.</i>. Rebbi Hoshaia took three wholesalers<sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote">Jastrow reads סיטונין for איסתוננסין. Buxtorf and Mussaphia read ἀστυνόμοι “street police”; R. M. Margalit reads “asthenics” who in his view are vegetarians and know the price of fruits.</i> [?] and redeemed on their word.
It is written (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 14:28" href="/Deuteronomy.14.28"><i>Deut</i>. 14:28</a>): “At the end of three years you shall take out all tithe of your produce, in that year, and deposit it in your gates.” I could think that once in a Sabbatical cycle you have to distribute the tithes including the tithe of the poor<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote">The tithe of the poor is mentioned separately since the paragraph in question introduces the tithe of the poor.</i>. The verse says “at the end of three years,” once in three years and not once in seven; i. e., in the third and the seventh<sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote">This formulation is inconsistent. It must either be the 3<sup class="footnote-marker">rd</sup> and the 6<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> year for the obligation of tithes, or the 4<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> and the 7<sup>th</sup> which are finally determined to be the times of delivery.</i>, twice in a Sabbatical cycle. Do I understand at New Year’s Day, that on New Year’s Day you have to distribute the tithes including the tithe of the poor? The verse says “at the end of three years.” “At the end” means at its conclusion you remove, you do not remove on New Year’s Day. If it is at the end of the year, I could understand that at the beginning of the fourth you have to remove the tithes including the tithe of the poor; the verse says (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 26:12" href="/Deuteronomy.26.12"><i>Deut</i>. 26:12</a>): “If you have finished tithing [all tithe of]<sup>78</sup><i class="footnote">In the masoretic text, missing in the quote.</i> your produce,” when you have tithed all your fruits. <sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote">From here on, including the tannaitic parts of the next two paragraphs, a similar text is in <i>Sifry Deut</i>. §109; in very shortened form also §302.</i> If it is when you have tithed all your fruits, could I understand even on Ḥanukkah<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote">Since Ḥanukkah is not connected with the agricultural year and is not a biblical holiday, its mention does not make much sense, in particular because the tithing year for trees and their fruits ends only on the 14<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Ševaṭ, more than a month and a half after the start of Ḥanukkah. The 15<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of Ševaṭ is mentioned as “New Year of trees” in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Rosh Hashanah 1:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Rosh_Hashanah.1.2.1">Mishnah <i>Roš Haššanah</i> 1:2</a>; in the opinion of the House of Shammai it is the first of Ševaṭ. This indetermination in itself disqualifies the New Year of trees as a biblical date. The discussion of the date is in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Rosh Hashanah 1:2:2-6" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Rosh_Hashanah.1.2.2-6"><i>Roš Haššanah</i> 1:2</a> (fol. 57a), Babli 14a.</i>? It says here, “at the end of;” it says further (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 26:12" href="/Deuteronomy.26.12"><i>Deut</i>. 26:12</a>): “At the end<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">In the biblical text, מקץ not מקצה.</i> of seven years, on the fixed time of the Sabbatical year, on the festival of booths.” Since “at the end” there means at a fixed time, so here also at a fixed time. Since there “at the end” means the holiday of booths, does it here also mean the holiday of booths? The verse says “if you have finished tithing all tithe of your produce,” when you have finished tithing all of your fruits? On Passover of the fourth year<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote">Since this is the first biblical holiday after the end of tithing fruits of the preceding year.</i>.
(<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 14:28" href="/Deuteronomy.14.28"><i>Deut</i>. 14:28</a>) “In that year” your are obliged to remove it but you are not obliged to remove it in any other year<sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote">In the <i>Sifry</i>, this sentence refers to a later discussion which in the Yerushalmi is purely amoraic.</i>. “In that year” you are obliged to remove; you are not required to remove vegetables which grew between New Year’s Day and Passover<sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">Since the vegetable belongs to the following, not to <i>this</i> year.</i>. The colleagues say, because he can make a declaration<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote">The declaration in the Temple that he fulfilled all his duties for tithes, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 26:13-15" href="/Deuteronomy.26.13-15"><i>Deut.</i> 26:13–15</a>.</i> [for the latter] only in the fifth year<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">Since the declaration is for <i>all</i> tithes, a declaration for part of the vegetables of a year is unacceptable.</i>. Rebbi Hila said, because it does not hinder the declaration in the fourth, only in the fifth. Where do they differ? If he transgressed and included it in his declaration. According to the colleagues it is invalid, according to Rebbi Hila is it valid<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">Since the declaration is for <i>all</i> tithes, a declaration for part of the vegetables of a year is unacceptable.</i>.
“In that year” you take it out from impure for pure but in other years you do not take it out from impure for pure. Rebbi Eleazar said, so is that <i>baraita</i>: “ ‘In that year’ you have to take it from an impure place to a pure but in other years you do not have to take it from an impure place to a pure.<sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote">The version of R. Eleazar is the version of <i>Sifry Deut</i>. 109; the first version is unintelligible. The extra “in this this year” mentioned in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 14:28" href="/Deuteronomy.14.28"><i>Deut</i>. 14:28</a> is interpreted to mean that in that year, the third (or sixth) of the Sabbatical cycles, <i>all</i> tithes have to be treated equally. Since Second Tithe, as long as it is not redeemed, has to be kept in purity (for consumption in Jerusalem), it follows that First Tithe also, which is to be given to the Levites, has to be kept in purity in these years. But this implies that in other years it may be left to become impure (alter heave was taken). This is taken to mean that in other years it should not be given to the Cohen together with the heave.</i>” This statement of Rebbi Eleazar follows the opinion that one does not give tithe to Cohanim. In the days of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi they wanted to vote not to give tithe to Cohanim. They said, why should we come to Rebbi Joshua ben Levi<sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote">Who was a Levite.</i> since he will help the Levites. He came and helped the Cohanim and said: In 24 places are Cohanim called Levites and this is one of them (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 44:15" href="/Ezekiel.44.15"><i>Ez</i>. 44:15</a>): “The Cohanim Levites, the descendants of Ẓadoq.<sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote">This is also his argument in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 86b" href="/Yevamot.86b">Babli <i>Yebamot</i> 86b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Chullin 24b" href="/Chullin.24b"><i>Ḥulin</i> 24b</a>.</i>”
Rebbi Binjamin bar Gidul and Rebbi Aḥa were sitting together and saying, is it not written (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 10:39" href="/Nehemiah.10.39"><i>Neh</i>. 10:39</a>): “The Cohen, descendant of Aaron, will share with the Levites in the Levite’s tithe”? To give him heave of the tithe. But is it not written (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 10:39" href="/Nehemiah.10.39"><i>Neh</i>. 10:39</a>): “The Levites shall bring [the tithe of]<sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote">From the masoretic text, missing in the quote, but carrying the essence of the proof. The first argument was that the verse associates Cohanim with Levites in receiving tithe. This was countered by the argument that Cohanim always receive the heave of the tithe and, therefore, are always getting part of the Levite’s tithe. That argument is disproved since the heave of the tithe is explicitly mentioned in the second part of the verse, “the Levites shall bring the tithe of the tithe to the Temple.”<br>This establishes that the right of Cohanim to take tithe was part of the constitution of Nehemiah. This is the accepted doctrine of the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 86b" href="/Yevamot.86b">Babli (<i>Yebamot</i> 86b</a>) which only discusses the reason behind the decree but does not deny that the right of Cohanim to tithe is purely rabbinical. The Yerushalmi denies this since it continues to find the pentateuchal basis for the rights of Cohanim.</i> the tithe”? Rebbi Ḥuna and the colleagues, one of them said “to the descendants of Levi”. Why does the verse say (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 18:21" href="/Numbers.18.21"><i>Num</i>. 18:21</a>): “And to the descendants of Levi<sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote">“And to the descendants of Levi I gave all tithes in Israel as inheritance.” The first argument is that the beginning “and” also includes the Cohanim. The second argument notes that the verse declares tithes to follow the laws of inheritance. If somebody in his will gives some special part to a son before the general distribution, that son is not excluded from taking part in the division of the inheritance. Therefore, the fact that the Cohanim got heave and the heave of the tithe does not exclude them from the ranks of “descendants of Levi”. If the verse had been addressed instead to “the Levites”, the Cohanim would have been excluded.</i>”? From here that one gives tithes to Cohanim. The other said, even if it were only written “to the descendants” one would give tithes to Cohanim. If somebody would say, my son X shall take property Y [before distribution] and the rest of my properties my sons shall inherit, does he not participate with them?
Rebbi Jonah gave his tithes to Rebbi Aḥa bar Ulla, not because he was a Cohen but because he studied Torah. What is the reason? (<a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 31:4" href="/II_Chronicles.31.4"><i>2Chr</i>. 31:4</a>) “He said to the people, the inhabitants of Jerusalem, to give the part of the Cohanim and the Levites, so they should be strong in the Torah of the Eternal.” Rebbi Huna did not take tithe, Rebbi Aḥa did not take tithe. Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba instructed himself to go outside the Land, not to take tithe<sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">The circumstances are narrated in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sheviit 3:1:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sheviit.3.1.2"><i>Ševi‘it</i> 3:1, Notes 5–6</a>.</i>. A person<sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote">Who was a Cohen.</i> asked Rebbi Samuel bar Naḥman who asked Rebbi Jonathan, may one take? He said to him, take, what fell to your tribe fell to you.
Rebbi Yannai ordered his relatives, when you lease<sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote">The Leyden ms. has חכר “to lease”, the Rome ms. and the Venice print חבר “to connect”. In view of H. L. Fleischer’s discussion (in Levy’s Dictionary, Vol. 2, p. 204b) of the original meaning of the Aramaic / Arabic root חכר as “keep tight, hold together, hold back” (in modern Arabic only “to hoard”) there is no difference of meaning involved.</i> a field, lease only from lay people since even if you say one does not give tithes to Cohanim you have to agree that one does not take his own<sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote">The tithe but not heave, cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Peah 1:5:5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Peah.1.5.5"><i>Peah</i> Chapter 1, Note 291</a>.</i> out of his hand. What is the reason? (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 18:26" href="/Numbers.18.26"><i>Num</i>. 18:26</a>) “If you take from the Children of Israel the tithe which I gave you from them as your inheritance, you should lift from it the heave of the Eternal, a tithe of the tithe.” From the Children of Israel you take out<sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote">If needed, by a court order.</i> but not from those contracting with Cohanim or Levites. It parallels what Rebbi Eleazar said, “if you take the tithe from the Children of Israel,” from the Children of Israel you take out but not from the Gentile<sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote">He holds that the produce of the Gentile farmer in the Land is exempt from heave and tithes. Since this is a matter of dispute between Tannaïm, cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Peah 4:6:9" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Peah.4.6.9"><i>Peah</i> Chapter 4, Notes 131–134</a>, one might read the statement here to say that tithe voluntarily given by a Gentile cannot be obtained from him by a court order; he may give to you but you cannot take from him.</i>.
Rebbi Abbahu said, Rebbi Joshua ben Ḥananiah<sup class="footnote-marker">99</sup><i class="footnote">A Levite. In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 86" href="/Yevamot.86">Babli, <i>Yebamot</i>86a/b</a>, the opponent of R. Eleazar ben Azariah is R. Aqiba at all stages.</i> and Rebbi Eleazar ben Azariah<sup class="footnote-marker">100</sup><i class="footnote">A Cohen, direct descendant of Ezra.</i> disagreed. Rebbi Joshua ben Ḥananiah said, one does not give tithe to Cohanim but Rebbi Eleazar ben Azariah said, one gives tithe to Cohanim. Rebbi Joshua ben Ḥananiah objected to Rebbi Eleazar ben Azariah: Is it not written (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 18:31" href="/Numbers.18.31"><i>Num</i>. 18:31</a>): “You shall eat it everywhere”, come and eat it by a grave<sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote">A place forbidden to Cohanim.</i>! He said to him, what means “everywhere”? In the courtyard<sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote">He must mean the courtyard of the priests since women are invited to enter the women’s courtyard and may enter the men’s courtyard for ceremonies required for sacrifices.</i> of the Temple. He retorted, but is it not written (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 18:31" href="/Numbers.18.31"><i>Num</i>. 18:31</a>): “You and your house<sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote">The expression “house” often is used to represent someone’s wife.</i>”? Does a woman enter the courtyard of the Temple? Rebbi Abba understood it from the following occasion: Rebbi Eleazar ben Azariah was used to take tithes from a certain garden. That garden had two exits, one to a place of impurity<sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup><i class="footnote">A cemetery.</i> and one open to a place of purity. Rebbi Aqiba went to him<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote">The owner of the vegetable garden. He persuaded him to leave only the cemetery door open and to lock the other.</i> and said, open this one and lock the other one. If he will come, tell him to come by that way. He also said, if he sends a student, tell him “you” is written<sup class="footnote-marker">106</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Demai 6:1:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Demai.6.1.3"><i>Demay</i> 6:1, Note 8</a>, that an emphasis on “you” means one personally unless an expression of inclusion is added; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Terumot 1:1:16" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Terumot.1.1.16"><i>Terumot</i> 1:1 Note 76</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 41b" href="/Kiddushin.41b">Babli <i>Qiddušin</i> 41b</a>.</i>. Rebbi Eleazar ben Azariah heard this and said, that is Aqiba ben Joseph’s whip. At that moment, Rebbi Eleazar ben Azariah returned all tithes he had taken<sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote">This remark, establishing the practice that tithes are not for Cohanim, is missing in the Babli which holds strongly that tithes should be given to Cohanim in preference to Levites.</i>. Rebbi Isaac bar Eleazar said, for dinner one has to fill up completely with wood fibers<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote">To make a point one has to take strong action immediately; later it is useless. The text is doubtful; the proverb appears three times; for סבא here one reads סמא in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Beitzah 2:3:2-3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Beitzah.2.3.2-3"><i>Beẓah</i> 2:3</a> and כסא in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Chagigah 2:3:2-5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Chagigah.2.3.2-5"><i>Ḥagigah</i> 2:3</a>.</i>; any coal which does not cause a burn at the beginning will not cause one.
Everybody agrees that bread and oil have to be removed, wine and spices are as if removed. Where do they disagree: A cooked dish the House of Shammai says one has to remove, but the House of Hillel say one does not have to remove<sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote">This is the discussion of the last sentence of Mishnah 6. A profane dish containing tithe oil is subject to removal, one containing tithe wine or spices is not since these are not recognizable. A dish made from tithe vegetables is not subject to removal since cooked vegetables are not the same as raw ones, according to the House of Hillel.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">117</sup><i class="footnote">This is the discussion of Mishnah 7.</i> What is the reason of the House of Shammai? (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 14:25" href="/Deuteronomy.14.25"><i>Deut</i>. 14:25</a>): “Bundle” only “the money in your hand.<sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote">Of Second Tithe. Since there is no Temple, the tithe cannot be eaten in Jerusalem. The House of Shammai hold that <a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 14:25" href="/Deuteronomy.14.25"><i>Deut</i>. 14:25</a> requires that any tithe produce which cannot be eaten in purity in the holy precinct has to be exchanged for money. Since that money cannot be used it must be destroyed or safely buried. The House of Hillel, the authors of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Maaser Sheni 1:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Maaser_Sheni.1.3.1">Mishnah 1:5</a>, hold that either the coins must be destroyed or the produce left to rot.</i>” What is the reason of the House of Hillel? Even if he exchanges, what good does it do<sup class="footnote-marker">118</sup><i class="footnote">Since the following injunction of the verse, to bring the money to the Holy Precinct, cannot be fulfilled, the entire verse becomes inapplicable.</i>?

Halakhah 4

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Rebbi Jehudah said, in earlier times they sent to the rural farmers, speed up your produce before the time of removal, until Rebbi Aqiba came and taught that any produce which did not reach the time of tithing is exempt from removal<sup class="footnote-marker">110</sup><i class="footnote">If it is exempt from removal, the fact that the farmer has untithed produce does not prevent him from reading the declaration of tithes (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 26:13-15" href="/Deuteronomy.26.13-15"><i>Deut</i>. 26:13–15</a>). The fact that R. Aqiba had to rule on the matter supports Maimonides (<i>Ma‘aser Šeni</i> 7:4) that the declaration should be made even if there is no Temple.</i>.<br>If somebody’s produce was far from him<sup class="footnote-marker">111</sup><i class="footnote">At the time of removal he has to tithe and transfer ownership of his tithes in order to be able to make the declaration.</i>, he has to give it a name. It happened that Rabban Gamliel was on a ship with the elders when Rabban Gamliel said, a tenth which I shall measure in the future is given to Joshua and its place is rented to him<sup class="footnote-marker">112</sup><i class="footnote">Real estate can be rented in the way it is acquired, by contract, payment, or taking actual possession. If real estate is acquired, movables on it can be acquired with it. Therefore, the future tithe is acquired by payment of the rent. Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 26b-27a" href="/Kiddushin.26b-27a">Babli <i>Qiddušin</i> 26b/27a</a>, <i>Baba Meẓi‘ai</i> 11a, and Rashi’s commentary there.</i>; another tenth which I shall measure in the future is given to Aqiba<sup class="footnote-marker">113</sup><i class="footnote">He was overseer of charities and as such could receive the tithe of the poor due at the time of removal.</i>; he should distribute it to the poor, and its place is rented to him. Rebbi Joshua said, a tenth<sup class="footnote-marker">114</sup><i class="footnote">The heave of the tithe given by the Levite to the Cohen.</i> which I shall measure in the future is given to Eleazar ben Azariah and its place is rented to him. They paid the rent to each other<sup class="footnote-marker">115</sup><i class="footnote">R. Eleazar ben Azariah to R. Joshua, RR. Joshua and Aqiba to Rabban Gamliel.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">119</sup><i class="footnote">This is the discussion of Mishnah 8. Since the declaration reads: “I removed the holy produce from the house”, meaning heave and tithes as well as fourth-year growth, why should untithed produce be subject to removal and hinder the declaration?</i> Is it not <i>ṭevel</i>? Rebbi Hila in the name of Samuel: This implies that <i>ṭevel</i> is called holy<sup class="footnote-marker">120</sup><i class="footnote">R. Aqiba agrees that <i>ṭevel</i> must be brought in order but he counsels not to bring new produce to the state of <i>ṭevel</i>.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">121</sup><i class="footnote">The text of the letters is also in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sanhedrin 1:2:2-35" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sanhedrin.1.2.2-35"><i>Sanhedrin</i> 1:2</a> (fol. 18d), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sanhedrin 2:2" href="/Tosefta_Sanhedrin.2.2">Tosephta <i>Sanhedrin</i> 2:6</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sanhedrin 11b" href="/Sanhedrin.11b">Babli <i>Sanhedrin</i> 11b</a>. The best text is preserved (although in Hebrew) from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 2" href="/Deuteronomy.2"><i>Midrash Tannaïm</i> in <i>Midrash Haggadol Deut</i>. (<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup> ed. S. Fisch, Jerusalem 1975</a>), pp. 597–598. There is an Introduction, a discussion between R. Neḥonia bar Haqanah and R. Joshua, whether the expression “I removed the holy produce from the house” implies that potentially titheable produce outside the house does not preclude the recitation of the declaration. R. Joshua replies that he never heard anything about it but he remembered Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel (I, later the president of the revolutionary government in the first war against the Romans) and Rabban Joḥanan ben Zakkai writing the letters in which they required tithing of unfinished produce, in accordance with R. Jehudah’s description of the earlier practice.</i> Rebbi Jehudah said, it happened that Rabban Gamliel<sup class="footnote-marker">122</sup><i class="footnote">While this is the text in both Talmudim and the Tosephta, and the Babli explicitly identifies this Rabban Gamliel with the head of the Synhedrion at Jabneh, for historical reasons the only acceptable reading is that of <i>Midrash Tannaïm</i>. Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel I (ben Simeon ben Hillel).</i> and the elders were sitting on the steps of the Hall on the Temple Mount and Joḥanan, the Cohen, their scribe, was sitting before them. They said to him, go and write:
To our brothers of Upper and Lower Galilee, may you have much peace. We inform you that the time of removal is approaching; take out tithes from the ripening vats<sup class="footnote-marker">123</sup><i class="footnote">A vat in which olives were stored before pressing and where they softened. On the basis of Arabic عطن one might translate “soaking vat”.</i> of olives. To our brothers of Upper and Lower South country, we inform you that the time of removal is approaching; take out tithes from the sheaves of grain<sup class="footnote-marker">124</sup><i class="footnote">Neither unthreshed grain nor unpressed oil olives are subject to heave and tithes in normal years. In <i>Midrash Tannaïm</i>, Rabban Simeon writes as excuse that he has to write because it is an old established practice.</i>. To our brothers of the diasporas of Babylonia, Media, Greece, and all other diasporas of Israel, may you have much peace. I am informing you that the lambs are young and the young pigeons small<sup class="footnote-marker">125</sup><i class="footnote">In the parallel sources, “it does not look like spring”. This letter is not in <i>Midrash Haggadol</i> since its subject is not tithes.</i>, so it is good in my eyes and the eyes of my colleagues to add thirty days to this year.
<sup class="footnote-marker">126</sup><i class="footnote">Here starts the discussion of Mishnah 9. Why did Rabban Gamliel choose the complicated way of giving to the Levite, could he not have given everything to the Cohen who would not have had to rent space for his heave of the tithe?</i> That means that one does not give tithe to Cohanim. There is a difference, since Rebbi Joshua ben Ḥananiah was there<sup class="footnote-marker">127</sup><i class="footnote">A poor Levite is preferable to a very rich Cohen under any circumstances.</i>. Rebbi Ḥananiah said, it means that Rabban Gamliel had to transfer<sup class="footnote-marker">128</sup><i class="footnote">The Mishnah requires only “to give a name”. But Rabban Gamliel actually transferred property rights.</i>. Rebbi Joshua<sup class="footnote-marker">129</sup><i class="footnote">An Amora whose identity cannot be determined. The editors of the Leyden ms. suggest to read צריך לזכות את רבי יהושע בפירות “he has to transfer the produce to R. Joshua (ben Ḥanania).”</i> said, for produce standing on the ground<sup class="footnote-marker">130</sup><i class="footnote">It was not yet in orderly heaps.</i>. Even if Rabban Gamliel’s box were standing in Rebbi Joshua’s house and he would say, he should acquire its tithe, would he have done anything if he did not label it<sup class="footnote-marker">131</sup><i class="footnote">Goods in a vessel of the giver (or seller) in the house of the recipient (or buyer) cannot be acquired by proxy unless their place is exactly described. If Rabban Gamliel’s grain had been in orderly heaps, he could have said the Northernmost 10% are First Tithe, the Southernmost 10% tithe of the poor. But in the situation he was in, he could only rent out ground for future use. This remark leads to the consideration of right of acquisition.</i>?
<sup class="footnote-marker">132</sup><i class="footnote">The text from here to the end of the Halakhah is also in <i>Peah</i> 4:6 and explained there, Notes 113–125. The question is about the power of a person to acquire property for a third party.</i> Rebbi Redifa said, Rebbi Jeremiah and Rebbi Yose disagree. One says, he who may take may acquire; the other says, he who may give may acquire. He who says “he who may take” certainly includes him who may give. He who says “he who may give,” excludes him who may take.
The following Mishnah disagrees with him who says that he who may take may acquire, since we have stated: “Give this divorce document to my wife,” because he may receive the divorce document of his minor daughter. “And the document of manumission to my slave,” since he may receive his own document of manumission. But did we not state: “Receive this divorce document for my wife or bring this divorce document to my wife; if he wants to change his mind … he may do so.” Is a slave empowered to bring a divorce document? Explain it by different cases contained in the Mishnah.
A Mishnah disagrees with him who says that he who may take may acquire, since we have stated there: “One tithe that I will measure in the future is given to Aqiba ben Joseph that he should let the poor acquire it, and its place is rented to him.” But is Rebbi Aqiba entitled to take? Explain it, before he got rich. And even if you say, after he became rich, when he was an administrator, and the hand of the administrator is equal to the hand of the poor.
The word of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi is that he who may take may acquire, since Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said: They disagree about a rich owner. But in the case of a poor owner, since he has the right to take it, the other person acquired it.

Halakhah 5

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> In the afternoon of the holiday<sup class="footnote-marker">133</sup><i class="footnote">This is the text in the Mishnah mss. of the Yerushalmi and Maimonides traditions, unspecified between first and last days of Passover. However, the Halakhah seems to presume a reading of “last day”.</i> they made the declaration. How was the declaration? (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 26:13" href="/Deuteronomy.26.13"><i>Deut</i>. 26:13</a>) “I removed the holy produce from the house,” is Second Tithe and fourth-year growth. “I gave it to the Levite,” is the Levite’s tithe. “Also I gave it,” includes heave and heave of the tithe. “To the sojourner, the orphan, and the widow,” is the tithe of the poor. “From the house,” is <i>ḥallah.</i> “Following Your entire Commandment which You commanded me;” therefore, if he gave Second Tithe before the First he cannot make the declaration. “I did not transgress Your Commandments,” I did not give from one kind for another, not from the harvested on the standing or from the standing on the harvested, not from new for old or from old for new. “And I did not forget,” to praise and mention Your Name over it.<br>(<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 26:14" href="/Deuteronomy.26.14"><i>Deut</i>. 26:14</a>) “I did not eat from it in my deep mourning;” therefore if he ate from it in deep mourning<sup class="footnote-marker">134</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Demai 1:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Demai.1.2.1"><i>Demay</i> Chapter 1, Note 70</a>.</i> he cannot make the declaration. “I did not remove any of it in impurity;” therefore if he separtated it in impurity he cannot make the declaration. “I did not give from it to the dead,” I did not buy from it a casket or shrouds for a dead person nor did I give it to other deep mourners. “I listened to the voice of the Eternal, my God,” I brought it to the Selected House<sup class="footnote-marker">135</sup><i class="footnote">A standard name for the Temple.</i>. “I did all You commanded me,” I enjoyed and gave joy to others with it<sup class="footnote-marker">136</sup><i class="footnote">Fulfilling part of the commandment (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 16:14" href="/Deuteronomy.16.14"><i>Deut</i>. 16:14</a>) “enjoy your holiday” with festive meals.</i>.<br>(<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 26:15" href="/Deuteronomy.26.15"><i>Deut</i>. 26:15</a>) “Look down from Your Holy Abode, from Heaven,” we did what You decided<sup class="footnote-marker">149</sup><i class="footnote">This use of גזר is in the sense of Biblical Hebrew “to cut” in the meaning of גזר דין = פסק דין “(judicial) decision”; not the rabbinical גדר = גור; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Demai 1:2:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Demai.1.2.4"><i>Demay</i> 1:2, Note 89</a>.</i> for us, You also do what You promised us: “Look down from Your Holy Abode, from Heaven, and bless Your people Israel” with sons and daughters, “and the land You gave us,” with dew, winds, rain and young of the domestic animals, “that You had sworn to our forefathers, a Land flowing with milk and honey” to give taste to the fruits<sup class="footnote-marker">150</sup><i class="footnote">The verse is the continuation of the declaration. The commentary is a paraphrase of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 28:4" href="/Deuteronomy.28.4"><i>Deut</i>. 28:4</a>.</i>.<br>Because of this<sup class="footnote-marker">168</sup><i class="footnote">The statement “the land You gave us” in the declaration.</i>, they said that Israel persons and <i>Mamzerim</i><sup class="footnote-marker">169</sup><i class="footnote">Children born from adultery or incest who are forbidden to marry regular Israelites (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 23:3" href="/Deuteronomy.23.3"><i>Deut</i>. 23:3</a>). Since the disability is hereditary, R. Ṭarphon in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 3:12:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.3.12.1">Mishnah <i>Qiddušin</i> 3:14</a> counsels male bastards to live with a non-manumitted slave girl and at the birth of a child (which is his biologically but not legally) manumit the child which by this act automatically becomes a full Jew free of his father’s disability. Today he would have to marry a non-Jewish woman and convert the child at birth.</i> may make the declaration but not proselytes and freed slaves who have no part in the Land. Rebbi Meïr says, also excluding Cohanim or Levites who did not receive any part of the Land. Rebbi Yose says, they have their cities with surroundings<sup class="footnote-marker">170</sup><i class="footnote">This was discussed in the preceding paragraph.</i>. <sup class="footnote-marker">171</sup><i class="footnote">From here it is also <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 9:10:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.9.10.1">Mishnah <i>Soṭah</i> 9:10</a>. The historical identity of this High Priest cannot be determined. {Cf. Eliahu Katz, “Who was Joḥanan the High Priest?” <i>Šanah bešanah</i> 1979, pp. 368–373 (Hebrew).} In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 9a" href="/Yoma.9a">Babli (<i>Yoma</i>9a</a>) it is reported that he acted as High Priest for 80 years; an assertion of doubtful accuracy like most historical stories in the Babli. According to a possible interpretation of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 13:6" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).13.6">Tosephta <i>Soṭah</i> 13:6</a>, he was the Hasmonean Joḥanan Hyrkanos; cf. Notes 188,189.</i> The High Priest Joḥanan disestablished the declaration of tithes. He also eliminated the arousers and the hitters<sup class="footnote-marker">172</sup><i class="footnote">This will be discussed in the Halakhah.</i>. Up to his days the hammer was hitting in Jerusalem<sup class="footnote-marker">173</sup><i class="footnote">This is explained only in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Makkot 11b" href="/Makkot.11b">Babli, <i>Makkot</i> 11b</a> and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 48a" href="/Sotah.48a"><i>Soṭah</i> 48a</a> and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 13:10" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).13.10">Tosephta <i>Soṭah</i> 13:10</a>. On the intermediate days of the holiday week urgent work may be done. But since metal work is very noisy, and Jerusalem was full of holiday pilgrims at these times, he decreed that, in Jerusalem only, noisy work should not be performed.</i> and in his days nobody had to ask about <i>demay</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Could he not make the declaration on the first day of Passover? So he should have something to eat for the holiday<sup class="footnote-marker">137</sup><i class="footnote">Since the declaration can only be recited if no Second Tithe, tithe money, and fourth-year growth are left, if he would make the declaration early he could not eat of his fruits or buy well-being sacrifices during the holiday.</i>. Could he not make the declaration in the morning? While he is commanded to eat.
It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">138</sup><i class="footnote">In the list of holy offerings that were removed before the declaration (Mishnah 10).</i>: “And First Fruits.” Who stated “First Fruits”? The rabbis. Who did not state “First Fruits”? Rebbi Simeon. As we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">139</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Bikkurim 2:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Bikkurim.2.2.1">Mishnah <i>Bikkurim</i>2:2</a>.</i>: “They are subject to removal but Rebbi Simeon frees them.”
“I gave it to the Levite,” from here that one does not give tithe to Cohanim<sup class="footnote-marker">140</sup><i class="footnote">This is the final word of the Yerushalmi in this matter.</i>.
Rebbi Jonah said, this means that if his <i>ṭevel</i> was burned he cannot make the declaration<sup class="footnote-marker">141</sup><i class="footnote">If he had <i>ṭevel</i>, he is required to give heave and tithes. If the produce was burned before he gave, he cannot fulfill the condition “I gave it to the Levite” and is disqualified. If his produce was burned before it became obligated, he never was under an obligation and may make the declaration for his other produce.</i>. Some Tannaïm say, all commandments in the Torah prevent him<sup class="footnote-marker">142</sup><i class="footnote">A literal interpretation of the text “I did not transgress Your Commandments.”</i>; some Tannaïm say, all commandments in the paragraph prevent him. Rebbi Aḥa bar Pappos<sup class="footnote-marker">143</sup><i class="footnote">A Babylonian, student of Rav Huna, known in Babylonia as “the long Rav Aḥa”, who immigrated into Galilee in the times of R. Immi and R. Abbahu.</i> asked before Rebbi Zeïra, even if he put on head phylacteries before phylacteries on his arm<sup class="footnote-marker">144</sup><i class="footnote">This is the proverbial description of a minor infraction, disregarding a positive commandment which is inferred from the structure of the text. The commandment to carry the words of the Torah on one’s hands and head is spelled out four times (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 13:9" href="/Exodus.13.9"><i>Ex</i>. 13:9</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 13:16" href="/Exodus.13.16">16</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 6:8" href="/Deuteronomy.6.8"><i>Deut</i>. 6:8</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 11:18" href="/Deuteronomy.11.18">11:18</a>). In each of these verses, hand is mentioned before head. It is inferred that putting them on the hand must precede putting them on the head.</i>? He said to him, that is also what I am thinking.
Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, he must say “<i>ḥallah</i> for all,” “heave for all.”<sup class="footnote-marker">145</sup><i class="footnote">The main place of this paragraph is at the end of the first Chapter of <i>Ḥallah</i>. It is inserted here as another example of rules to be followed to be able to make the declaration. It was established in the first Chapter of <i>Terumot</i> that heave may be given only from produce whose location is exactly pinpointed. Therefore, in taking heave one must declare all produce that should be freed by this heave. <i>Ḥallah</i> is called “heave” in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 15:19-20" href="/Numbers.15.19-20"><i>Num</i>. 15:19–20</a>; it has to follow the rules of heave.</i> “To YHWH,” that is the particular Name<sup class="footnote-marker">146</sup><i class="footnote">It is written about <i>ḥallah</i>(<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 15:19" href="/Numbers.15.19"><i>Num</i>. 15:19</a>): “Lift a heave to YHWH.” About heave, it is written (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 18:12" href="/Numbers.18.12"><i>Num</i>. 18:12</a>): “Their first gifts which they will give to YHWH”. It is inferred that in separating heave of <i>ḥallah</i>, God may not be addressed as Elohim (which in absence of a definite article or other identifyer only means “extraordinary power”), but only as YHWH (in its substitute pronunciation) which is His particular Name.</i>. From where that he did not do anything until he left some [as profane]? The verse says (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 15:21" href="/Numbers.15.21"><i>Num</i>. 15:21</a>): “Of the beginning” and not all the beginning<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Challah 1:6:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Challah.1.6.1">Mishnah <i>Ḥallah</i>1:9</a>: He who says, everything on my threshing floor shall be heave, all my dough shall be <i>ḥallah</i>, did not say anything unless he leaves a [profane] remainder.”</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">148</sup><i class="footnote">This is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Maaser Sheni 2:1:9" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Maaser_Sheni.2.1.9">Chapter 2, Notes 34–35</a> and refers to the prohibition to use any tithe or tithe money for funeral rites.</i> From where that he would transgress a positive commandment? Rebbi Eleazar in the name of Rebbi Simai (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 26:14" href="/Deuteronomy.26.14"><i>Deut</i>. 26:14</a>): “Nor did I give from it to the dead.” Where do we hold? If it were to bring a casket and shrouds for him, that were also forbidden for a living person! If something is forbidden for the living, not so much more for the dead? What is something which is permitted for the living but prohibited for the dead? That is anointing!
Rebbi Huna bar Aḥa<sup class="footnote-marker">151</sup><i class="footnote">He is not otherwise known.</i> in the name of Rebbi Alexandros: Come and see the power of those who keep the Commandments because all “lookings down” in the Torah<sup class="footnote-marker">152</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 18:16" href="/Genesis.18.16"><i>Gen</i>. 18:16</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 19:28" href="/Genesis.19.28">19:28</a> (Sodom), 26:8 (Abimelekh and Rebekka), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 14:24" href="/Exodus.14.24"><i>Ex</i>. 14:24</a> (Egyptians on the Sea). This refers only to <i>hiph‘il</i> of שקף.</i> are curses but this one is in the language of blessing. Rebbi Yose ben Ḥanina said, not only that but it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">153</sup><i class="footnote">Starting words of the next paragraph guaranteeing instant response.</i> (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 26:16" href="/Deuteronomy.26.16"><i>Deut</i>. 26:16</a>) “this day,” the condition of every day.
Rebbi Judah bar Pazi started<sup class="footnote-marker">154</sup><i class="footnote">Started a sermon.</i> with this: (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 71:16" href="/Psalms.71.16"><i>Ps</i>. 71:16</a>): “I shall come in strength, Eternal, God.<sup class="footnote-marker">155</sup><i class="footnote">While the verse is quite clear: “When I reach old age, o Master, Eternal, I shall remember only Your justice!”, it is taken here out of context to note that it seems to be possible to come in strength before the Eternal.</i>” It is written (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Zechariah 4:14" href="/Zechariah.4.14"><i>Zach</i>. 4:14</a>): “These are the two oil-sons who stand over the Lord of all the earth.” Rebbi Abbahu said, Rebbi Joḥanan and Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish disagree. One says, these are the ones who come in novitiate<sup class="footnote-marker">156</sup><i class="footnote">From Latin <i>tiro, -onis</i> “novice, recruit” to mean “come without accumulated merit before the Eternal. {The commentaries and dictionaries all derive the word from Greek τυραννίς, because of a similar homily in the next paragraph using באין בזרוע “being strong-armed”. But then it should read טוּרוניא and a clear meaning of the sentence can only be obtained by distorting the meaning of the word.}</i> before the Holy One, praised be He. The other one says, these are the ones who come by the power of [kept] commandments and good deeds before the Holy One.
Rav had flax which was blighted<sup class="footnote-marker">157</sup><i class="footnote">In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Chullin 85b-86a" href="/Chullin.85b-86a">Babli, <i>Ḥulin</i> 85b–86a</a>, the story is told of R. Ḥiyya and Rebbi. There, the decision goes against R. Meïr.</i>. He asked the elder Rebbi Ḥiyya, may one slaughter a bird and mix its blood with flax seed? He said, a cadaver<sup class="footnote-marker">158</sup><i class="footnote">He could not use the blood of a regularly slaughtered kosher bird since that has to be covered with earth (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 17:13" href="/Leviticus.17.13"><i>Lev</i>. 17:13</a>). It seems that his agricultural practice did not allow using the blood of a non-kosher bird.</i>. Why did he not say to him, a torn one<sup class="footnote-marker">159</sup><i class="footnote">A kosher bird regularly slaughtered but which was found to have a bodily defect which made it forbidden. In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Chullin 6:2" href="/Mishnah_Chullin.6.2">Mishnah <i>Ḥulin</i> 6:2</a>, the anonymous majority (which in the Babli is identified as R. Simeon and his followers) free the blood from the obligation of covering since the bird is not to be eaten but R. Meïr requires covering.</i>? Because of Rebbi Meïr, for Rebbi Meïr said [the blood of] a torn [bird] must be covered. But did not Rebbi Immi say in the name of Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish: From the time when they came from the diaspora, flax was never blighted and wine never became vinegar; they considered this to be due to the merit of the Great Rebbi Ḥiyya and his sons<sup class="footnote-marker">160</sup><i class="footnote">How could Rav’s flax be blighted when his uncle’s merit should have shielded it.</i>. But Rav is like (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 46:12" href="/Isaiah.46.12"><i>Is</i>. 46:12</a>): “Listen to me, mighty of heart, who are far from charity!”<sup class="footnote-marker">161</sup><i class="footnote">In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 17b" href="/Berakhot.17b">Babli, <i>Berakhot</i> 17b</a>, the explanation is by either Rav and Samuel or R. Joḥanan and R. Eleazar.</i> Rebbi Abbahu said, Rebbi Joḥanan and Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish disagree. One says, all the world depend on charity but these on strong arms<sup class="footnote-marker">162</sup><i class="footnote">Since Rav only trusted his own merit, he was not shielded by another’s merit.</i>. But the other one said that all good things and consolations come to the world in their merit but they themselves do not profit at all<sup class="footnote-marker">163</sup><i class="footnote">According to the Babli, no flax in all the Land of Israel was blighted in the times of R. Ḥiyya except his own.</i>. For example Mar Zuṭra<sup class="footnote-marker">164</sup><i class="footnote">He seems to be identical with Mar Zuṭra Ḥasida mentioned in the Babli, whose time cannot be ascertained. What is told here of the Babylonian Mar Zuṭra is told in the Babli (<i>loc. cit</i>.) of the Palestinian R. Ḥanina ben Dosa.</i> who prayed and fasted for others but for himself he never fasted.
<sup class="footnote-marker">165</sup><i class="footnote">The origin of this paragraph is in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Makkot 2:6:2-7:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Makkot.2.6.2-7.4"><i>Makkot</i> 2:7</a> (fol. 32a); the statement is alluded to in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 9:2:2-9" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.9.2.2-9"><i>Soṭa</i> 9:2</a> (fol. 23c). Here, it refers to the disagreement between R. Yose and R. Meïr on the status of Levites and Cohanim, whether they may read the declaration which refers to “the land You gave us.” If the Levitical cities and the cities of refuge were parcelled out to their inhabitants, then they own land given by God. But if the cities were tribal property and the houses given to the inhabitants as living quarters by the tribal council, not as property, then individual Levites and Cohanim never obtained land and cannot read the declaration.</i> It was stated: They were given to be distributed, the words of Rebbi Jehudah. Rebbi Yose said, they were given as dwellings. It turns out that Rebbi Jehudah holds with Rebbi Yose<sup class="footnote-marker">166</sup><i class="footnote">The name tradition is garbled. In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Makkot 2:6:2-7:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Makkot.2.6.2-7.4"><i>Makkot</i> 2:7</a>, the text reads: It turns out that Rebbi Yose holds with Rebbi Jehudah. The reference is to the statement of R. Yose in the next Mishnah, which parallels R. Yehudah’s opinion in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Makkot 2:6:2-7:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Makkot.2.6.2-7.4"><i>Makkot</i> 2:7</a>. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Makkot 2:7:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Makkot.2.7.1">Mishnah <i>Makkot</i> 2:15</a> (Babli 2:8) reads: “They were paying rent to the Levites, the words of Rebbi Jehudah; Rebbi Meïr says they were not paying rent.” Therefore, the text of the preceding sentence must be: R. Meïr says, they were given as dwellings.</i> and Rebbi Meïr follows his own opinion as we have stated: “They<sup class="footnote-marker">167</sup><i class="footnote">In all old sources, the verb is in the feminine 3<sup>rd</sup> person plural. The object of the Mishnah are homicides which by the court in whose jurisdiction the crime was committed were sentenced to exile in a city of refuge. Rashi explains that the question was whether the homicide’s home town has to pay rent in the city of refuge (presumably to be charged to the criminal’s family). R. Jacob Ettlinger (<i>Arukh leNer Makkot</i> 13a) notes that Rashi is forced to explain this because “city” עיר is feminine. It is assumed here that the explanation is that lodging a criminal in a private home clearly requires payment but if the cities of refuge were given as tribal property subject to a lien that they had to accept all homicides, then no extra rent is due. Rava in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Makkot 13a" href="/Makkot.13a">Babli, <i>Makkot</i>13a</a>, holds that in a city of refuge no rent can be due; the only question was about the other 42 Levitic cities which might give temporary refuge to the homicide between crime and trial. This cannot be the position of the Yerushalmi.</i> were paying rent to the Levites, the words of Rebbi Jehudah; Rebbi Yose says they were not paying rent.”
Rebbi Jeremiah, Rebbi Ḥiyya in the name of Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish: Our Mishnah<sup class="footnote-marker">174</sup><i class="footnote">Which states that Joḥanan the High Priest abolished the recitation of the declaration. He held that people who do not follow the rules cannot make the declaration and giving tithe to Cohanim breaks the rules. In order not to be inquisitive he let nobody recite.</i> after the people were suspected of giving tithe to Cohanim. There is support for Rebbi Joḥanan in one and disagreement with him in one. Disagreement with him as we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">175</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yevamot 9:5:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yevamot.9.5.1">Mishnah <i>Yebamot</i> 9:6</a>. In the interpretation of the Yerushalmi, one speaks about the daughter of a Cohen preliminarily married to a Levite, who has lost her Cohen status and not yet acquired Levitic status. In the interpretation of the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 86a" href="/Yevamot.86a">Babli (<i>Yebamot</i>86a</a>) which holds that tithes should regularly be given to Cohanim, the Mishnah is explained away: The daughter of a Cohen married to a Levite may eat tithes but she cannot receive tithes from an Israel as a precaution since an Israel woman married to a Cohen should not accept heave or tithe from an Israel since we are afraid her husband might die without issue and then she would be barred from heave and tithes.</i>: “Similarly, the daughter of a Cohen [married] to a Levite should eat neither heave nor tithe.” We understand that she should not eat heave<sup class="footnote-marker">176</sup><i class="footnote">Since legally she is married; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Peah 6:2:6" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Peah.6.2.6"><i>Peah</i> 6, Note 46</a>.</i>. But tithe any way you take it, if she is a Cohen’s daughter she should eat, if she is a Levite’s wife she should eat. Rebbi Hila in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: [It follows] him who says one does not give tithe to Cohanim. That means, he himself<sup class="footnote-marker">177</sup><i class="footnote">If R. Joḥanan considers the Mishnah contrary to his position, he must hold that Cohanim may receive tithe according to biblical law.</i> says one gives heave to Cohanim.
It supports him because he says it is all praise, as Rebbi Joḥanan said<sup class="footnote-marker">178</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 13:10" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).13.10">Tosephta <i>Soṭah</i> 13:10</a>; a slightly different text <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 48a" href="/Sotah.48a">Babli <i>Soṭa</i> 48a</a>. The passage is explained in the Introduction to Tractate <i>Demay</i>.</i>, Joḥanan the High Priest sent and checked in all localities of Israel and found that they separated only Great Heave. But First and Second Tithes some were separating and some did not. He said, since [omitting] First Tithe is a deadly sin and [omitting] Second Tithe [implies] the sin of <i>ṭevel</i>, a person should give a name to heave<sup class="footnote-marker">179</sup><i class="footnote">This must be the instruction to the farmer, not the buyer who can be sure that heave was taken. The ms. evidence of the Tosephta does not permit deleting the reference to heave.</i> and heave of the tithe and give them to the Cohen; Second Tithe he exchanges for coins. About the remaining tithe of the poor, he who has a claim on another person must bring proof.
Why should he not make the declaration<sup class="footnote-marker">180</sup><i class="footnote">Why should the necessity of introducing <i>demay</i> lead to the disestablishment of the declaration? The remedy indicates that the not too religiously scrupulous could omit the incriminating passages without anybody noticing, which shows that Joḥanan’s order was not followed in subsequent generations.</i>? Rebbi Hila said, he causes anger before the Omnipresent by saying “I did” when he did not. If it is so, he who separated should make the declaration, he who did not separate should not make the declaration, as we have stated: “Up to ‘Look down’ they were saying it in an undertone, from ‘Look down’ onwards in a high voice.”
“The arousers.” Those who were saying (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 44:24" href="/Psalms.44.24"><i>Ps</i>. 44:24</a>): “Be roused, why do You sleep, o Eternal, please awake, do not abandon forever.<sup class="footnote-marker">181</sup><i class="footnote">According to Babli <i>Sota</i>(<i>loc. cit.</i>) and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 13:9" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).13.9">Tosephta <i>Soṭah</i> 13:9</a>, this was a daily song of the Levites in the Temple.</i>” Does there exist sleep before the Omnipresent? Has it not already been said (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 121:4" href="/Psalms.121.4"><i>Ps</i>. 121:4</a>): “Lo, He will not slumber nor sleep, the Guardian of Israel!” Why does the verse say (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 78:65" href="/Psalms.78.65"><i>Ps</i>. 78:65</a>): “Like a sleeper awoke the Eternal, like a hero exhilarated by wine.” But in a symbolic way it is as if sleep were before Him when Israel is in trouble and the other peoples are at ease. So it says (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Job 17:2" href="/Job.17.2"><i>Job</i> 17:2</a>): “When they apostasize, My eye will rest.”
“The hitters.” Those who were hitting the calf between its horns<sup class="footnote-marker">182</sup><i class="footnote">In the Rome ms.: בין חרצו “in its depression.” To stun the animal before slaughter. According to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 13:10" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).13.10">Tosephta <i>Soṭah</i> 13:10</a>, this was usually done with animals brought to pagan slaughter.</i>. Joḥanan the High Priest said to them, how long will you feed torn animals to the altar<sup class="footnote-marker">183</sup><i class="footnote">If the membrane covering the brain is torn, the animal is forbidden food.</i>? He went and made them rings<sup class="footnote-marker">184</sup><i class="footnote">To immobilize the neck of the animal to be slaughtered. The word in parentheses is not in the Rome ms.</i>. Rebbi Abba in the name of Rebbi Jehudah: He made rings for them, rings wide below and narrow at the top.
“Up to his days the hammer was hitting in Jerusalem,”<sup class="footnote-marker">173</sup><i class="footnote">This is explained only in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Makkot 11b" href="/Makkot.11b">Babli, <i>Makkot</i> 11b</a> and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 48a" href="/Sotah.48a"><i>Soṭah</i> 48a</a> and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 13:10" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).13.10">Tosephta <i>Soṭah</i> 13:10</a>. On the intermediate days of the holiday week urgent work may be done. But since metal work is very noisy, and Jerusalem was full of holiday pilgrims at these times, he decreed that, in Jerusalem only, noisy work should not be performed.</i> up to his early days. “And in his days nobody had to ask about <i>demay</i>” because he sent out teams<sup class="footnote-marker">185</sup><i class="footnote">Who made the rounds through all agricultural areas and saw to it that every farmer tithed.</i>.
The word of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi implies some<sup class="footnote-marker">186</sup><i class="footnote">Of the recorded actions of the High Priest Joḥanan.</i> are censure and some praise. Since Rebbi Yose said in the name of Rebbi Tanḥum bar Ḥiyya, Rebbi Ḥizqiah, Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Yose, Rebbi Tanḥum bar Ḥiyya in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi, originally tithe was split into three parts. One third to his acquaintances among Cohanim and Levites, one third to the public treasury, one third to the poor and the fellows in Jerusalem. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, a person who went to court in Jerusalem, up to three letters<sup class="footnote-marker">187</sup><i class="footnote">Summons to the opposing party to appear before the court.</i> he paid for himself, from there on from the public treasury. When Eleazar ben Paḥora<sup class="footnote-marker">188</sup><i class="footnote">In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 66a" href="/Kiddushin.66a">Babli (<i>Qiddušin</i> 66a</a>) he is called Eleazar ben Po‘era, described as a Sadducee, and placed in Alexander Yannai’s time.</i> and Judah ben Patora<sup class="footnote-marker">189</sup><i class="footnote">In the parallel in <i>Soṭah</i> 9:10 he is called בן פכורה. They might have been Cohanim and taking the tithe by force for themselves but more likely were royal officials who took all for the public treasury.</i> came, they took it by force and it would have been in his hand to stop this but he did not but disestablished the declaration of tithes<sup class="footnote-marker">190</sup><i class="footnote">Since the tithe was taken by force, the biblical rules could not be kept. If the identification of this High Priest with Joḥanan Hyrkanos is true, he himself would have been a beneficiary of the corrupt system.</i>, and this is for censure. But the arousers for praise and the hitters for praise.
“Up to his days the hammer was hitting in Jerusalem,” up to his early days<sup class="footnote-marker">191</sup><i class="footnote">In that case, he would be praised for stopping the practice. If he tolerated it and only his successors abolished it, he would be mentioned for censure.</i>. Rebbi Ḥasida<sup class="footnote-marker">192</sup><i class="footnote">A fourth generation Amora, asking not only R. Ḥizqiah but also R. Yose.</i> asked Rebbi Ḥizqiah, is it not reasonable to the end of his days. He said, I also am of that opinion.
{What means] <i>demay</i>? Rebbi Yose in the name of Rebbi Abbahu, Rebbi Ḥizqiah in the name of Rebbi Jehudah ben Pazi: Maybe he put in order, maybe he did not put in order<sup class="footnote-marker">193</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. Introduction to Tractate Demay, p. 348.</i>.
